25:T5713,<entryFree id="n8734" key="حَلَّ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">حَلَّ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حل</orth>
                  </form>, (S, Mgh, Msb, K,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="Halu3a">حَلُلَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حَلٌّ</foreign>, (S, Mgh, Msb,) <hi rend="ital">He untied,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">undid,</hi> (K, TA,) or <hi rend="ital">opened,</hi> (S,) a knot: (S, Mgh, Msb, K:) this is the primary signification. (Er-Rághib, TA.) Hence, <foreign lang="ar">يَا عَاقِدُ ٱذْكُرْ حَلًّا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">O tyer of a knot, bear in mind</hi> the time of <hi rend="ital">untying:</hi> or <foreign lang="ar">حَابِلُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">O binder,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tyer, of the rope:</hi> (see art. <foreign lang="ar">حبل</foreign>:)] (S, TA:) or, as IAar relates it, <foreign lang="ar">يا حَامِلُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">O loader</hi>]: a prov., applied to the consideration of results; because a man may tie a load too tightly; and when he desires to untie it, may injure himself and his camel. (TA. [See also a similar saying below, in the second paragraph.]) And <foreign lang="ar">الشُّفْعَةُ كَحَلِّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">العِقَالِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The right of preemption is like the untying of the cord with which a camel's fore shank and arm are bound together</hi>]: meaning that it is accomplished as quickly and easily as the <foreign lang="ar">عقال</foreign> is untied: the explanation that it passes away quickly, like the camel when his <foreign lang="ar">عقال</foreign> is untied, is improbable. (Mgh, Msb. *) And hence the saying [in the Kur xx. 28], <foreign lang="ar">وَ ٱحْلُلْ عُقْدَةً مِنْ لِسَانِى</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  [<hi rend="ital">And loose Thou an impediment of,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">from, my tongue</hi>]. (Er-Rághib, TA.) The pass. is pronounced by some <foreign lang="ar">حُلَّ</foreign>, and by others <foreign lang="ar">حِلَّ</foreign>: thus in the saying of El-Farezdak, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">فَمَا حِلَّ مِنْ جَهْلٍ حُبَى حُلَمَائِنَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَ لَا قَابِلُ المَعْرُوفِ فِينَا يُعَنَّفُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">And the garments of our forbearing men by which they support themselves in sitting by binding them,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">making them tight, round the shanks and back are not loosed through ignorance, nor is the accepter of the benefit, among us, reproached</hi>]; the kesreh of the first <foreign lang="ar">ل</foreign> [in the original form <foreign lang="ar">حُلِلَ</foreign>] being transferred to the <foreign lang="ar">ح</foreign>: but Akh heard it pronounced in this instance <foreign lang="ar">حُلَّ</foreign>; and some, he says, in this word, and in others like it, as <foreign lang="ar">رُدَّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">شُدَّ</foreign>, only impart to the dammeh somewhat of the sound of kesreh, by the pronunciation termed <foreign lang="ar">إِشْمَام</foreign>. (S.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [<hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, dissolved, melted,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">liquefied,</hi> a thing; as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8734-1" target="حلّل" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">تَحْلِيلٌ</foreign>, often said of a medicine as meaning <hi rend="ital">it acted as a dissolvent.</hi>] <foreign lang="ar">حُلَّ</foreign>, (M, K,) inf. n. as above, (TA,) meaning <hi rend="ital">It was dissolved, melted,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">liquefied,</hi> is said of anything congealed, frozen, or solid. (M, K.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  [<assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He solved</hi> a problem, or riddle, &amp;c.          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">He analyzed</hi> a thing; as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8734-2" target="حلّل" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, inf. n. as above.]          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَلَّ اليَمِينَ</foreign>: see 2.          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  From <foreign lang="ar">حَلُّ الأَحْمَالِ عِنْدَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">النُّزُولِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The untying, unbinding,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">loosing, of the loads on the occasion of alighting</hi>], <foreign lang="ar">حَلَّ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حُلُولٌ</foreign>, came to be used alone as meaning <foreign lang="ar">نَزَلَ</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">He alighted;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">descended and stopped</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sojourned</hi> or <hi rend="ital">abode</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lodged</hi> or <hi rend="ital">settled;</hi> and simply <hi rend="ital">he took up his abode;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">he abode, lodged,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">settled;</hi> in a place]. (Er-Rághib, TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">حَلَّ بِالْمَكَانِ</foreign> (S, K) or <foreign lang="ar">بِالْبَلَدِ</foreign>, (Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">حَلَّ المَكَانَ</foreign> (S, Mgh, * K) or <foreign lang="ar">البَلَدَ</foreign>, (Msb,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="Halu3a">حَلُلَ</orth>
                  </form> (S, Msb, K) and      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar" marker="Hali3a">حَلِلَ</orth>
                  </form>, (K,) both of which forms of the aor. are mentioned by Ibn-Málik, (TA,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حُلُولٌ</foreign> (S, Mgh, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">حَلٌّ</foreign> (S, K) and <foreign lang="ar">حَلَلٌ</foreign>, which is extr., (K,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَحَلٌّ</foreign> (S, TA) and <foreign lang="ar">مَحِلٌّ</foreign>; (TA;) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8734-3" target="احتلّ" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n8739"/>بِهِ</foreign> (S, * K) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8734-4" target="احتلّهُ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>; (K;) meaning <foreign lang="ar">نَزَلَ بِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He alighted,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">descended and stopped</hi> &amp;c. (as above), <hi rend="ital">in the place</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the country</hi> or <hi rend="ital">town</hi> &amp;c.]. (Msb, K, TA.) And in like manner, <foreign lang="ar">حَلَّ بِالقَوْمِ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">حَلَّ القَوْمَ</foreign> (S, ISd, TA) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8734-5" target="احتلّ" n="5" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar" select="n8739"/>بِهِمْ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8734-6" target="احتلّهُمْ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n8739"/></foreign> (ISd, TA) [<hi rend="ital">He alighted,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">descended and stopped &amp;c., at,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in, the abode of the people</hi> or <hi rend="ital">party</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">حَلَّ إِلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">القَوْم</foreign> signifies the same. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">حُلَّ المَكَانُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The place was alighted in,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">taken as an abode;</hi> (TA;) <hi rend="ital">was inhabited.</hi> (K.) [Hence, in philosophy, <foreign lang="ar">حُلُولٌ</foreign> signifies <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Temporary</hi> or <hi rend="ital">separable,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">permanent</hi> or <hi rend="ital">inseparable, indwelling</hi> or <hi rend="ital">inbeing:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">حَلَّ بِهِ</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">فِيهِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">It had,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became in the condition of having, such indwelling</hi> or <hi rend="ital">inbeing in it.</hi> And <foreign lang="ar">حَلَّ بِهِ</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">فِيهِ</foreign> is often said of joy and grief and the like, meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">It took up its abode in him.</hi> And <foreign lang="ar">حَلَّ <ref cref="n8734-7" target="مَحَلَّ" n="7" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>كَذَا</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">It took,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">occupied, the place of such a thing.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  And hence, (TA,) <foreign lang="ar">حَلَّ الهَدْىُ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) aor.

                  <form>

                  <form>

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n8771-1" target="مُحَلَّلٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n8769"/></foreign> applied to a place: (S, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">chosen as a place of rend="ital">abounding with herbage wholesome to the cattle.</hi> (TA.)
